actbusy
ActBusy Script File
// "act busy name"		This is the name that a mapmaker must specify in the hint node.
// 	"busy_anim"			"Activity Name".
// 	"entry_anim"		"Activity Name"
// 	"exit_anim"			"Activity Name"
// 	"busy_sequence"		"Sequence Name". If specified, this is used over the activity name. Specify it in the hint node.
// 	"entry_sequence"	"Sequence Name". If specified, this is used over the entry anim.
// 	"exit_sequence"		"Sequence Name". If specified, this is used over the exit anim.
// 	"min_time"			"Minimum time to spend in this busy anim"
// 	"max_time"			"Maximum time to spend in this busy anim"	0 = only stop when interrupted by external event
// 	"interrupts"		One of:
// 						"BA_INT_NONE"		break out only when time runs out. No external influence will break me out.
// 						"BA_INT_DANGER"		break out of this anim only if threatened
// 						"BA_INT_PLAYER"		break out of this anim if I can see the player, or I'm threatened
// 						"BA_INT_AMBUSH"		someone please define this - I have no idea what it does
// 						"BA_INT_COMBAT"		break out of this anim if combat occurs in my line of sight (bullet hits, grenades, etc), -OR- the max time is reached

toolimages:model_editor/phys_sphere.png
toolimages:model_editor/phys_capsule.png
toolimages:model_editor/phys_hull.png
toolimages:model_editor/phys_mesh.png
toolimages:model_editor/phys_box.png
toolimages:model_editor/phys_compound.png
toolimages:model_editor/grey_empty_set.png
toolimages:model_editor/shape_list_rot.png
Mathematically precise sphere. Sphere is the absolute cheapest collision primitive. It will roll very smoothly. Example: a volleyball.
Mathematically precise capsule (pill-shaped, cylinder with rounded ends, both ends having the same radius). Capsule is the second-cheapest primitive. It can be arbitrarily elongated, which makes it the perfect choice for ragdoll body parts or elongated animated/kinematic objects like turnpikes or individual bars in a cage. 
Convex hull, the most complex shape that can still be dynamically simulated and have collision. If your input mesh has holes, concavities, non-manifold geometry, multiple pices etc., they will all be shrink-wrapped into one convex polygonal shape. Example: a flowerpot full of dirt (without dirt, there would be holes or concavities).
Static Mesh
Mesh is the most arbitrary form of collision. It <b>cannot</b> be dynamically simluated in Rubikon, i.e. it <font color=red><b>cannot roll or tumble</b></font> around and move on its own without animation. All triangles of your input geometry will be faithfully reproduced in collision, so use degenerate or non-manifold or non-closed geometry at your own risk. Example: a piece of level geometry, like a building. <font color=red><big>Do not use this for prop_physics</big></font>, because it will sink through objects.
Box will find the top, bottom and sides from your input geometry, but will not use it other than for computing dimensions. Box is a special case of the Convex Hull, and is relatively cheap to simulate. Example: a crate, or a cereal box.

1OnSelectionChanged()
(Compound)
Sometimes you need a dynamically simluated object (a thing that can tumble, roll, fall and hit something else) that has holes or concavities or is otherwise non-convex. In those cases, you can compose a few pieces of geometry, each individually convex, but that comprise a complex shape. Example: a table that has legs and top, that you want to be able to knock over for it to tumble around. The legs and top would be 4 boxes and 1 box, respectively, and would constitute a compound shape.
(No Collision)
Do not create any collision
(Shape List)
A list of shapes
